101 def __init__( 3.10.macos-latest.c3.10.macos-latest.py3.10.ubuntu-latest.c3.10.ubuntu-latest.py3.10.windows-latest.c3.10.windows-latest.py3.8.macos-latest.c3.8.macos-latest.py3.8.ubuntu-latest.c3.8.ubuntu-latest.py3.8.windows-latest.c3.8.windows-latest.py3.9.macos-latest.c3.9.macos-latest.py3.9.ubuntu-latest.c3.9.ubuntu-latest.py3.9.windows-latest.c3.9.windows-latest.py

102 self, data_file=_DEFAULT_DATAFILE, data_suffix=None, cover_pylib=None, 

103 auto_data=False, timid=None, branch=None, config_file=True, 

104 source=None, source_pkgs=None, omit=None, include=None, debug=None, 

105 concurrency=None, check_preimported=False, context=None, 

106 messages=False, 

107 ): # pylint: disable=too-many-arguments 

108 """ 

109 Many of these arguments duplicate and override values that can be 

110 provided in a configuration file. Parameters that are missing here 

111 will use values from the config file. 

112 

113 `data_file` is the base name of the data file to use. The config value 

114 defaults to ".coverage". None can be provided to prevent writing a data 

115 file. `data_suffix` is appended (with a dot) to `data_file` to create 

116 the final file name. If `data_suffix` is simply True, then a suffix is 

117 created with the machine and process identity included. 

118 

119 `cover_pylib` is a boolean determining whether Python code installed 

120 with the Python interpreter is measured. This includes the Python 

121 standard library and any packages installed with the interpreter. 

122 

123 If `auto_data` is true, then any existing data file will be read when 

124 coverage measurement starts, and data will be saved automatically when 

125 measurement stops. 

126 

127 If `timid` is true, then a slower and simpler trace function will be 

128 used. This is important for some environments where manipulation of 

129 tracing functions breaks the faster trace function. 

130 

131 If `branch` is true, then branch coverage will be measured in addition 

132 to the usual statement coverage. 

133 

134 `config_file` determines what configuration file to read: 

135 

136 * If it is ".coveragerc", it is interpreted as if it were True, 

137 for backward compatibility. 

138 

139 * If it is a string, it is the name of the file to read. If the 

140 file can't be read, it is an error. 

141 

142 * If it is True, then a few standard files names are tried 

143 (".coveragerc", "setup.cfg", "tox.ini"). It is not an error for 

144 these files to not be found. 

145 

146 * If it is False, then no configuration file is read. 

147 

148 `source` is a list of file paths or package names. Only code located 

149 in the trees indicated by the file paths or package names will be 

150 measured. 

151 

152 `source_pkgs` is a list of package names. It works the same as 

153 `source`, but can be used to name packages where the name can also be 

154 interpreted as a file path. 

155 

156 `include` and `omit` are lists of file name patterns. Files that match 

157 `include` will be measured, files that match `omit` will not. Each 

158 will also accept a single string argument. 

159 

160 `debug` is a list of strings indicating what debugging information is 

161 desired. 

162 

163 `concurrency` is a string indicating the concurrency library being used 

164 in the measured code. Without this, coverage.py will get incorrect 

165 results if these libraries are in use. Valid strings are "greenlet", 

166 "eventlet", "gevent", "multiprocessing", or "thread" (the default). 

167 This can also be a list of these strings. 

168 

169 If `check_preimported` is true, then when coverage is started, the 

170 already-imported files will be checked to see if they should be 

171 measured by coverage. Importing measured files before coverage is 

172 started can mean that code is missed. 

173 

174 `context` is a string to use as the :ref:`static context 

175 <static_contexts>` label for collected data. 

176 

177 If `messages` is true, some messages will be printed to stdout 

178 indicating what is happening. 

179 

180 .. versionadded:: 4.0 

181 The `concurrency` parameter. 

182 

183 .. versionadded:: 4.2 

184 The `concurrency` parameter can now be a list of strings. 

185 

186 .. versionadded:: 5.0 

187 The `check_preimported` and `context` parameters. 

188 

189 .. versionadded:: 5.3 

190 The `source_pkgs` parameter. 

191 

192 .. versionadded:: 6.0 

193 The `messages` parameter. 

194 

195 """ 

196 # data_file=None means no disk file at all. data_file missing means 

197 # use the value from the config file.

328 def _should_trace(self, filename, frame): 3.10.macos-latest.c3.10.macos-latest.py3.10.ubuntu-latest.c3.10.ubuntu-latest.py3.10.windows-latest.c3.10.windows-latest.py3.6.macos-latest.c3.6.macos-latest.py3.6.ubuntu-latest.c3.6.ubuntu-latest.py3.6.windows-latest.c3.6.windows-latest.py3.7.macos-latest.c3.7.macos-latest.py3.7.ubuntu-latest.c3.7.ubuntu-latest.py3.7.windows-latest.c3.7.windows-latest.py3.8.macos-latest.c3.8.macos-latest.py3.8.ubuntu-latest.c3.8.ubuntu-latest.py3.8.windows-latest.c3.8.windows-latest.py3.9.macos-latest.c3.9.macos-latest.py3.9.ubuntu-latest.c3.9.ubuntu-latest.py3.9.windows-latest.c3.9.windows-latest.pypypy3.macos-latest.pypypy3.ubuntu-latest.py

329 """Decide whether to trace execution in `filename`. 

330 

331 Calls `_should_trace_internal`, and returns the FileDisposition. 

332 

333 """ 

334 disp = self._inorout.should_trace(filename, frame) 

335 if self._debug.should('trace'): 

336 self._debug.write(disposition_debug_msg(disp)) 

337 return disp

339 def _check_include_omit_etc(self, filename, frame): 3.10.macos-latest.c3.10.macos-latest.py3.10.ubuntu-latest.c3.10.ubuntu-latest.py3.10.windows-latest.c3.10.windows-latest.py3.6.macos-latest.c3.6.macos-latest.py3.6.ubuntu-latest.c3.6.ubuntu-latest.py3.6.windows-latest.c3.6.windows-latest.py3.7.macos-latest.c3.7.macos-latest.py3.7.ubuntu-latest.c3.7.ubuntu-latest.py3.7.windows-latest.c3.7.windows-latest.py3.8.macos-latest.c3.8.macos-latest.py3.8.ubuntu-latest.c3.8.ubuntu-latest.py3.8.windows-latest.c3.8.windows-latest.py3.9.macos-latest.c3.9.macos-latest.py3.9.ubuntu-latest.c3.9.ubuntu-latest.py3.9.windows-latest.c3.9.windows-latest.pypypy3.macos-latest.pypypy3.ubuntu-latest.py

340 """Check a file name against the include/omit/etc, rules, verbosely. 

341 

342 Returns a boolean: True if the file should be traced, False if not. 

343 

344 """ 

345 reason = self._inorout.check_include_omit_etc(filename, frame) 

346 if self._debug.should('trace'): 

347 if not reason: 

348 msg = f"Including {filename!r}" 

349 else: 

350 msg = f"Not including {filename!r}: {reason}" 

351 self._debug.write(msg) 

352

676 def combine(self, data_paths=None, strict=False, keep=False): 3.10.macos-latest.c3.10.macos-latest.py3.10.ubuntu-latest.c3.10.ubuntu-latest.py3.10.windows-latest.c3.10.windows-latest.py3.6.macos-latest.c3.6.macos-latest.py3.6.ubuntu-latest.c3.6.ubuntu-latest.py3.6.windows-latest.c3.6.windows-latest.py3.7.macos-latest.c3.7.macos-latest.py3.7.ubuntu-latest.c3.7.ubuntu-latest.py3.7.windows-latest.c3.7.windows-latest.py3.8.macos-latest.c3.8.macos-latest.py3.8.ubuntu-latest.c3.8.ubuntu-latest.py3.8.windows-latest.c3.8.windows-latest.py3.9.macos-latest.c3.9.macos-latest.py3.9.ubuntu-latest.c3.9.ubuntu-latest.py3.9.windows-latest.c3.9.windows-latest.pypypy3.macos-latest.pypypy3.ubuntu-latest.py

677 """Combine together a number of similarly-named coverage data files. 

678 

679 All coverage data files whose name starts with `data_file` (from the 

680 coverage() constructor) will be read, and combined together into the 

681 current measurements. 

682 

683 `data_paths` is a list of files or directories from which data should 

684 be combined. If no list is passed, then the data files from the 

685 directory indicated by the current data file (probably the current 

686 directory) will be combined. 

687 

688 If `strict` is true, then it is an error to attempt to combine when 

689 there are no data files to combine. 

690 

691 If `keep` is true, then original input data files won't be deleted. 

692 

693 .. versionadded:: 4.0 

694 The `data_paths` parameter. 

695 

696 .. versionadded:: 4.3 

697 The `strict` parameter. 

698 

699 .. versionadded: 5.5 

700 The `keep` parameter. 

701 """

870 def report( 3.10.macos-latest.c3.10.macos-latest.py3.10.ubuntu-latest.c3.10.ubuntu-latest.py3.10.windows-latest.c3.10.windows-latest.py3.8.macos-latest.c3.8.macos-latest.py3.8.ubuntu-latest.c3.8.ubuntu-latest.py3.8.windows-latest.c3.8.windows-latest.py3.9.macos-latest.c3.9.macos-latest.py3.9.ubuntu-latest.c3.9.ubuntu-latest.py3.9.windows-latest.c3.9.windows-latest.py

871 self, morfs=None, show_missing=None, ignore_errors=None, 

872 file=None, omit=None, include=None, skip_covered=None, 

873 contexts=None, skip_empty=None, precision=None, sort=None 

874 ): 

875 """Write a textual summary report to `file`. 

876 

877 Each module in `morfs` is listed, with counts of statements, executed 

878 statements, missing statements, and a list of lines missed. 

879 

880 If `show_missing` is true, then details of which lines or branches are 

881 missing will be included in the report. If `ignore_errors` is true, 

882 then a failure while reporting a single file will not stop the entire 

883 report. 

884 

885 `file` is a file-like object, suitable for writing. 

886 

887 `include` is a list of file name patterns. Files that match will be 

888 included in the report. Files matching `omit` will not be included in 

889 the report. 

890 

891 If `skip_covered` is true, don't report on files with 100% coverage. 

892 

893 If `skip_empty` is true, don't report on empty files (those that have 

894 no statements). 

895 

896 `contexts` is a list of regular expressions. Only data from 

897 :ref:`dynamic contexts <dynamic_contexts>` that match one of those 

898 expressions (using :func:`re.search <python:re.search>`) will be 

899 included in the report. 

900 

901 `precision` is the number of digits to display after the decimal 

902 point for percentages. 

903 

904 All of the arguments default to the settings read from the 

905 :ref:`configuration file <config>`. 

906 

907 Returns a float, the total percentage covered. 

908 

909 .. versionadded:: 4.0 

910 The `skip_covered` parameter. 

911 

912 .. versionadded:: 5.0 

913 The `contexts` and `skip_empty` parameters. 

914 

915 .. versionadded:: 5.2 

916 The `precision` parameter. 

917 

918 """

920 self,

1107 """Call this at Python start-up to perhaps measure coverage. 

1108 

1109 If the environment variable COVERAGE_PROCESS_START is defined, coverage 

1110 measurement is started. The value of the variable is the config file 

1111 to use. 

1112 

1113 There are two ways to configure your Python installation to invoke this 

1114 function when Python starts: 

1115 

1116 #. Create or append to sitecustomize.py to add these lines:: 

1117 

1118 import coverage 

1119 coverage.process_startup() 

1120 

1121 #. Create a .pth file in your Python installation containing:: 

1122

1124 

1125 Returns the :class:`Coverage` instance that was started, or None if it was 

1126 not started by this call. 

1127 

1128 """

1134 # This function can be called more than once in a process. This happens
